I was popping Motrin left and right when I finally called Kaiser and they recommended physical therapy. Then I was referred to Smile Bright Family Dentistry and Dr. Chahal shared he could make a few adjustment, and he did. And that was it!! Within a few weeks later my TMJ pain went away. My whole life I've been told I had a small mouth, and I've always dreaded going to the dentist. Dr. Chahal cured me from that. He and his entire stuff are wonderful. If anyone's ever loathed going to the dentist from fear of pain or of bad results you have to give Dr. Chahal a try! You will have no regrets!< /text>< pictures>

<Text>Serene park for hiking camping and more! A numbers of trails are closed due to the fires in 2020.  Some of the bridges are also out for the season, and should be back in business by April.  RV (no hookups) and tent camping are available and can be reserved through reserveCalifornia.com. Special call out to the park staff.  Answers your questions and support you with a smile.  Be sure to ask for recommendations on trails, as they know the park very well. No cell signal, so be sure to let your family/friends before you set out for this park!)<//Text>< pictures>

< text>
The camp host is a real good guy.
He is very helpful and very friendly.
He has a good dog( Fiddler ) that is cool too.
Have been camping here while working in Stanford. Nicer than a hotel, and cheaper too.
Site 39 is the best, two flat places for tents and away from everyone.  Can‚Äôt see another site from 39. 3 is good too.
Reservations are made on the web. A little tricky to navigate.
Bathrooms near 52 are the better of the two. Use the handicap shower in back, it gets the best hot water.

UPDATE:
Campgrounds are now closed.
I stayed in 10 different sites over the summer.
Stay away from 29, noise from out building is terrible.

<userid>103630387222880212398<//userid>< Rating>

<Response>None<//Response><date>1501200249015<//date><review>Beautiful campground nestled in a redwood forest.  I stayed in site 41, which was shady, albiet not as private as some of the other sites.

Sites are equipped with a fire ring with a heavy duty grate for cooking.  All sites have metal lockers to keep your food in.  Garbage bins are close to sites so it's easy to just throw out garbage as you generate it.

Modern restroom facilities are available, as well as showers.  Showers require quarters. It's $0.25 per minute and you start with $0.50/2 min.  Make sure to bring quarters; camp office hours are irregular and they don't have a lot of change.

Firewood is available for $10/bundle.  Make sure to have exact change or pay with credit.   Suggest stocking up to ensure you don't run out.

There are plenty of varying length hiking trails.  I highly recommend the one that goes to Tip Toe falls.   Walking along Pescsdero Creek is also very nice.

A great campground for peace and quiet.  People seem to go to sleep at a decent time and there are no problems with loud noises.

A good choice for families too (lots of kids around).

Oh and there is no cell service here. This is nice as it lets you disconnect.  You can get Verizon 1x by the camp office.  For stronger service you need to drive out a ways.  Just something to know in terms of communicating with others you're going to meet there, etc.</review>< pics>
None</pics>

<Review>I'll start with the positive. This place doesn't cost much to camp, it has a ranger station that supplies camp-like items and tourist trinkets, and it offers nature hikes. You can bring your doggos, but just make sure to keep them on their leashes. You cannot bring them on the trails however. This place is about two hours from Santa Cruz, but is about twenty minutes, maybe less, from Los Gatos. The bathrooms are separated by sex and are stalled (there's only three). There are outlets in the bathroom, so that was an unexpected surprise. There is also only two showers per camp site area. This place didn't seem too popular when I went, so I wouldn't expect much of a crowd. Mosquitoes swarm in hives where I was at. No matter how many citronella candles were lit and Off I was wearing, it still wasn't enough. There isn't any cell service and the emergency phone outside the ranger station is useless. If you do stay here,  just know that there are mountain lions in this area. One came in our camp site (we think it was after our two small dogs who were in our tent). It took over an hour for the ranger to get to the camp after we finally were able to call 911. We had heard the mountain lion screaming for the past couple of nights and it finally wandered into our tent. If you don't know what they sound like, youtube it. It's the scariest sound you will ever hear. What may have been scarier was the fact the ranger didn't know they made that sound. Also during our stay there was a pervert who tried something on a seven-year-old. The cops came and the little girl was okay, but there were no rangers anywhere. The only reason why we knew about it was because we pulled in when the sheriffs were there. I can't recommend this place. Also, there were no redwoods anywhere. Just a typical forest campground.<//Review>< pics>

<pictures>None<//pictures><Review>This is a very pleasant coffee shop that gives off a completely different  vibe than what I see these days. There isn't much table space so it is not really the same sit around and talk vibe that I would get from a Starbucks. Sit in inner part of the cafe and it is very serene. They play very soft instrumental music and I find it to be very relaxing. I order the dirty chai tea and a breakfast burrito, just a perfect combination for a quick breakfast.

The cafe does face the train tracks directly so you do get the rumbling train every few minutes but this was not a big deal to me.

<Name>Steven ‚ÄúLeon‚Äù Cooper<//Name><time>1528828613493</time><Rate>5</Rate>< text>
I have been coming to this location for 4 years now and have never been let down by the excellent customer service of the owner and the employees. The food is not winning any awards or anything, but it's just meant to be a convenient, fast meal that's a tad healthier than your average burger or other fast food. I especially love Flame Broiler's choice of sauces, they're particularly good when mixed together (The "Magic" Sauce and the standard red "Hot" sauce). Overall I greatly enjoy the food, especially the beef. My only real complaint is that the drink lids are ridiculously hard to fit onto the cups without making a mess. The service here is extremely fast, a line out the door is hardly anything to worry about unless you're ordering something truly obscure from the menu (which is rare as they have a very simplified menu with mostly the basic Flame Broiler options that every location has).<//text>

< Review>
There are a lot of trails you can enjoy. Great place for hiking, running, mountain biking and horseback riding. Some parts of the trails are steep, like the first half of Joice trail starting at Benal ranch, again Joice trail coming up from the east to Vista loop trail, Boundary trail near the Coyote Peak and the first half of Mine trail at Nored ranch . If you want thrill of MTB'ing, try the rocky ridge trail. Most of the trails have no shade, so you need sunscreen and lots of water. Sometimes you can see snakes, wild turkeys, dears along the trail. A couple of months ago, I spotted a group of wild boars.</Review>

< text>
This is a great safe place to go hiking. If you have a dog you are able to bring them as long as they are on a leash. Luckily every Trail is easy to find and even easier to find your way back. < Review>
Consistently see several groups of deer walking about freely and unbothered. The park is not busy and often feels like no one else is there. Very clean and well maintained. Bit of a steep climb to get to if biking to it. The trails inside the park are optimum for mountain biking (not for road bikes).
Restroom is also very well maintained.

San Jose seriously needs to revisit their drone restrictions. This park is vast and would see more use if it were a drone friendly park.</Review>

<review>Absolutely amazing county park in the heart of Silicon Valley with a diverse network of trails overseeing the valley and adjoining Santa Teresa Golf Course. This park is incredibly accessible for most San Jose residents via Bernal Road and is a great way to get back to nature and escape the everyday hustle and bustle of city life. The trail up to Coyote Peak is quite challenging but offers those who make it to the top a majestic view all the way to San Francisco on a clear day. One of my favorite Bay Area parks by far.<//review><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< resp>

< text>
I lived with in walking distance to this park, I was able to find parking outside the park, sometimes it gets busy and you would have to park at the curb.
It would take me about 1.5 hours to do my usual hike. You will find small deer, turkeys, boars, quale, rattle snakes, etc.
At the entrance they have a spot with a map and information about the type of wild animals you can encounter. They have pamphlets that come with a map and information you can take.
They also provide hiking sticks it's a first come first serve.
I would totally recommend it!< /text>

<UserId.>110698033859740861390<//UserId.><gmap_id>0x808e2fc181066781:0xc7069f6213d5dbba< /gmap_id>< Review>
This park is a nice place to go hiking and mountain biking. Sometimes you will see deer, turkey, or quail around this area. There many also be snakes on the trail. Be careful as they may attack you if you get too close. I try to leave a good distance when walking past them. They will simply slither away if you do so. In the spring, there is a variety of different wildflowers. Sometimes the flowers will be in big patches. Sometimes there will be nice sunsets in the park also.</Review>

A large county park with numerous walking/ bike trails. Nice vistas of Santa Clara Valley, depending on the trails you take. BBQ pits, water faucets and large covered seating area. Restrooms near by. Wildlife... Turkeys, deer, wild pig, coyote and rare mountain lion. Dogs allowed but on leash. (They may chase wildlife so keep on leash, coyote and boar not to be messed with! Mountain lion info near restrooms) Good parking. Ticket kiosk, per car, near entrance. Outdoor movies shown in summertime.<//text>

< user>
104042685529602206608< /user>
<username>Marco Paganini</username><Time>1461389869308</Time>< rating>
5<//rating>
< review>
Santa Teresa is my favorite park in San Jose. The park occupies a sizable area and has a fair amount of trails for hikers, bikers, and horse riders. The highest point in the park (Coyote Peak) offers a nice view of San Jose (but be prepared for the steep climb, especially if you're biking there.)

Santa Teresa is usually not very crowded, even on weekends. Weekdays are especially nice for those who enjoy activities like animal and bird watching, or a lone bike ride.

Unlike many other parks, leashed dogs *are* allowed here (but please, make sure your dog is on a leash!).The park also offers (clean) public restrooms and a large covered area which can be reserved for parties.

For mountain bikers, the park offers a wide range of biking trails, ranging from almost flat and easy to rocky and technical. No matter how experienced you are, you can always create a route that will get you entertained (and tired).

The only thing I miss in this park is a large body of water. There are a few seasonal streams running through the park, but no lakes.

The parking lot is fairly large, and parking was $6 last time I checked. Rangers do check the place and will give you tickets if you don't pay the parking fees or park your car on the road.</review>

(Translated by Google) Come to Santa Teresa County Park, located ten miles south of downtown San Jose in the Santa Teresa Mountains. This 1,673-acre park has a rich history and spectacular views from the trails above the Almaden and Santa Clara valleys. The secluded highland valley of the park provides a quiet episode for exploring the natural surroundings of the surrounding developed areas. Santa Teresa County Park is located at the southern end of Santa Teresa. The park can be accessed from the Alma Mountain Valley or Santa Clara Valley. From the Santa Clara Valley, take the US 101 or 85 motorway to the Bernal Road exit. Drive 1.3 miles west along Bernal Road and cross Santa Teresa Avenue to Santa Teresa. Bernal Road continues through the park's Santa Teresa Golf Club and enters the hills. Located on Bernal Road, Pueblo Day Use Area is set in a small open valley on a hill.
